## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt represents the equation of motion. The acceleration typically depends on position x through nonlinear restoring forces, on velocity v through damping terms, and possibly on time t through external driving forces.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (linear restoring + periodic driving)
- Driven damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing with driving)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (time-modulated stiffness)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v (mixed coupling term)
- Softening spring with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- General polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (quadratic + cubic nonlinearity)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium; even powers (x²) indicate asymmetric potentials
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v represent energy dissipation (damping) or injection; sign determines stability
- Terms like (1 - c*x²)*v indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-sustained oscillators (limit cycles)
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicates external periodic driving forces
- Cubic position terms x³ with same sign as linear term x indicate hardening spring; opposite sign indicates softening spring
- Products x*v or x²*v represent nonlinear coupling between potential and kinetic energy channels
- Absence of explicit time dependence t suggests an autonomous system where energy is conserved or dissipated monotonically
- Rational forms like x/(1 + c*x²) can represent bounded restoring forces that saturate at large displacements
